!important;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eA SYN flood attack is a form of denial-of-service (DoS) attack that targets the way computers connect to each other over the internet. When one computer (the client) wants to talk to another (the server), it starts by sending a “SYN” (synchronize) request. The server replies with a “SYN-ACK” (synchronize-acknowledge) response. The client then completes the connection by sending back an “ACK” (acknowledgement) message.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" requests. The server responds to each request; However, the attacker never sends the final ACK message. As a result, the server keeps waiting for the missing ACK responses, which uses up its resources. This causes the server to wait, filling up its connection capacity and making it unable to handle legitimate requests, leading to a denial of service (DoS).\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"1322185288\" paraeid=\"{b32da8e4-3ad4-401f-938b-01a87cc7f715}{207}\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eAs the targeted server becomes overwhelmed and unresponsive, the attack disrupts legitimate user access. Incoming SYN Packets:\u003c/strong\u003e An unexpected spike in SYN packets is a prime sign of a SYN flood. This is the main characteristic of the attack, where the attacker floods the server with SYN requests.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUnusually High Number of Half-Open TCP Connections\u003c/strong\u003e: The target server will accumulate many incomplete connections, where the server is waiting for the final step of the handshake to complete, but the client never responds with the final ACK.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResource Exhaustion\u003c/strong\u003e: SYN flood attacks often lead to resource fatigue on the target server, as it is forced to allocate resources for each incomplete connection.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUnusual Source IPs or IP Spoofing\u003c/strong\u003e: Attackers often spoof the source IP addresses in a SYN flood; this leads to a high number of unique or suspicious IP addresses sending SYN requests to the target.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003ch2\u003ePreventing a SYN Flood Attack\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"1126731896\" paraeid=\"{2c5726c3-b205-48a1-b27b-ab2bdfaabe02}{90}\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:19.55px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eWhile Forcepoint offers numerous security capabilities, such as traffic behavior analysis and deep packet inspection (DPI) to analyze the content of incoming traffic and monitor overall network activity, we also provide specific features that protect against SYN Flood Attacks. These features include:\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:19.55px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:276}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRate-Based DoS Protection\u003c/strong\u003e: This limits the number of incoming SYN requests per second, helping to prevent SYN flood attacks by automatically blocking traffic that exceeds predefined policy thresholds, ensuring the server isn't overwhelmed by too many requests.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLimit for Half-Open TCP Connections\u003c/strong\u003e: This feature sets a threshold for the number of incomplete connections the firewall will allow, preventing the server from becoming flooded with half-open connections, which is a typical result of a SYN flood attack.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSlow HTTP Request Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: This detects slow or delayed HTTP requests, which are sometimes used in combination with SYN floods to exhaust server resources. It helps to identify and block malicious traffic that attempts to tie up server resources with slow, incomplete HTTP transactions.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSYN Flood Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: By specifically targeting SYN flood attacks, this feature detects unusually high rates of SYN packets and automatically triggers defenses to block or mitigate the attack, preventing the server from being overwhelmed with half-open connections.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSlow HTTP Request Blacklist Timeout\u003c/strong\u003e: When slow or malicious HTTP requests are detected, this feature adds offending IPs to a blacklist for a specified timeout period, preventing them from making further connections and mitigating the impact of SYN floods and other slow attacks.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTCP Reset Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: This feature can detect abnormal TCP session resets (RST packets) and automatically reset malicious or incomplete connections, closing half-open sessions caused by SYN flood attacks and freeing up server resources.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv that targets the way computers connect to each other over the internet. When one computer (the client) wants to talk to another (the server), it starts by sending a “SYN” (synchronize) request. The server replies with a “SYN-ACK” (synchronize-acknowledge) response. The client then completes the connection by sending back an “ACK” (acknowledgement) message.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"151703544\" paraeid=\"{b32da8e4-3ad4-401f-938b-01a87cc7f715}{175}\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eThe attacker overwhelms the server with many\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun Highlight SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:rgb(245, 246, 246);color:rgb(51, 51, 51);font-family:Arial, Arial_EmbeddedFont, Arial_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11.5pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:19.425px;margin:0px;outline:transparent solid 1px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eSYN requests. The server responds to each request; However, the attacker never sends the final ACK message. As a result, the server keeps waiting for the missing ACK responses, which uses up its resources. This causes the server to wait, filling up its connection capacity and making it unable to handle legitimate requests, leading to a denial of service (DoS).\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"1322185288\" paraeid=\"{b32da8e4-3ad4-401f-938b-01a87cc7f715}{207}\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eAs the targeted server becomes overwhelmed and unresponsive, the attack disrupts legitimate user access. This results in downtime, loss of service, and potential damage to the company's reputation. In high-traffic environments, such as online retailers and online banking, the attack strains network resources, degrades performance, and leads to customer dissatisfaction.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:18.3458px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;color:rgb(15, 71, 97);font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;Aptos Display_EmbeddedFont\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;Aptos Display_MSFontService\u0026quot;, sans-serif;font-size:16pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:26.9792px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"none\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\" data-ccp-parastyle=\"heading 2\"\u003eHow to spot a SYN Flood Attack\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;color:rgb(15, 71, 97);font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;Aptos Display_EmbeddedFont\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;Aptos Display_MSFontService\u0026quot;, sans-serif;font-size:16pt;line-height:26.9792px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;134245418\u0026quot;:true,\u0026quot;134245529\u0026quot;:true,\u0026quot;335559738\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:80}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"ListContainerWrapper SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;margin:0px;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHigh Volume of Incoming SYN Packets:\u003c/strong\u003e An unexpected spike in SYN packets is a prime sign of a SYN flood. This is the main characteristic of the attack, where the attacker floods the server with SYN requests.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUnusually High Number of Half-Open TCP Connections\u003c/strong\u003e: The target server will accumulate many incomplete connections, where the server is waiting for the final step of the handshake to complete, but the client never responds with the final ACK.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResource Exhaustion\u003c/strong\u003e: SYN flood attacks often lead to resource fatigue on the target server, as it is forced to allocate resources for each incomplete connection.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUnusual Source IPs or IP Spoofing\u003c/strong\u003e: Attackers often spoof the source IP addresses in a SYN flood; this leads to a high number of unique or suspicious IP addresses sending SYN requests to the target.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003ch2\u003ePreventing a SYN Flood Attack\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"1126731896\" paraeid=\"{2c5726c3-b205-48a1-b27b-ab2bdfaabe02}{90}\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"TextRun SCXW224461866 BCX8 NormalTextRun\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-variant-ligatures:none !important;line-height:19.55px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-contrast=\"auto\" xml:lang=\"EN-US\" lang=\"EN-US\"\u003eWhile Forcepoint offers numerous security capabilities, such as traffic behavior analysis and deep packet inspection (DPI) to analyze the content of incoming traffic and monitor overall network activity, we also provide specific features that protect against SYN Flood Attacks. These features include:\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"EOP SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;font-family:Aptos, Aptos_EmbeddedFont, Aptos_MSFontService, sans-serif;font-size:11pt;line-height:19.55px;margin:0px;padding:0px;user-select:text;\" data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:276}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRate-Based DoS Protection\u003c/strong\u003e: This limits the number of incoming SYN requests per second, helping to prevent SYN flood attacks by automatically blocking traffic that exceeds predefined policy thresholds, ensuring the server isn't overwhelmed by too many requests.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eLimit for Half-Open TCP Connections\u003c/strong\u003e: This feature sets a threshold for the number of incomplete connections the firewall will allow, preventing the server from becoming flooded with half-open connections, which is a typical result of a SYN flood attack.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSlow HTTP Request Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: This detects slow or delayed HTTP requests, which are sometimes used in combination with SYN floods to exhaust server resources. It helps to identify and block malicious traffic that attempts to tie up server resources with slow, incomplete HTTP transactions.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSYN Flood Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: By specifically targeting SYN flood attacks, this feature detects unusually high rates of SYN packets and automatically triggers defenses to block or mitigate the attack, preventing the server from being overwhelmed with half-open connections.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSlow HTTP Request Blacklist Timeout\u003c/strong\u003e: When slow or malicious HTTP requests are detected, this feature adds offending IPs to a blacklist for a specified timeout period, preventing them from making further connections and mitigating the impact of SYN floods and other slow attacks.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTCP Reset Sensitivity\u003c/strong\u003e: This feature can detect abnormal TCP session resets (RST packets) and automatically reset malicious or incomplete connections, closing half-open sessions caused by SYN flood attacks and freeing up server resources.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"OutlineElement Ltr SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;clear:both;cursor:text;direction:ltr;margin:0px;overflow:visible;padding:0px;position:relative;user-select:text;\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"Paragraph SCXW224461866 BCX8\" style=\"-webkit-tap-highlight-color:transparent;-webkit-user-drag:none;background-color:transparent;color:windowtext;font-kerning:none;font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;margin:0px 0px 10.6667px;overflow-wrap:break-word;padding:0px;text-align:left;text-indent:0px;user-select:text;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\" paraid=\"1460237954\" Forcepoint detects anomalies such as a surge in SYN requests or unusual request sources. But the repercussions of using unapproved software to interact with sensitive information can understandably have far-reaching consequences for data security and compliance.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSavvy IT teams are getting ahead of these risks through better visibility and control of shadow AI—here’s how.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eThe Four Main Risks of Shadow AI\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eUnderstanding where risk resides in shadow AI is the first step in preventing it. While shadow AI presents unique challenges to data security, it is fundamentally no different than the unapproved cloud app usage that every IT admin knows all too well.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUnsanctioned software usage inherently\u003cstrong\u003e creates risk of data loss\u003c/strong\u003e because the security team hasn’t had a chance to evaluate the controls the vendor has in place to prevent data loss. Where there are countless mature organizations like Microsoft, Salesforce or ServiceNow that have extensive documentation on how they protect sensitive information used on their platforms, there are – especially in the case of AI startups – thousands more that do not.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSimilarly, if the security team does not have a tight handle on how and where AI is interacting with data, then \u003cstrong\u003ecompanies risk non-compliance\u003c/strong\u003e with local and international regulations. Legislators are increasingly seeking to put \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/impact-of-legislation-on-ai\"\u003eguardrails on how AI stores and uses data\u003c/a\u003e, and organizations bear the burden of ensuring the data they are responsible for is handled correctly.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOf course, there are also risks that are unique to AI. For instance: some artificial intelligence models are trained through user input. In cases where employees share financial records or customer information for help with analysis or responses, this may inadvertently \u003cstrong\u003espur a data leak\u003c/strong\u003e. In those cases, companies need to ensure that the AI doesn’t train using that data – a tough task with shadow AI – or it may provide the information as part of an answer to another user.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe challenges businesses face isn’t only limited to the input of AI, but the output as well. When it comes to \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/use-case/chatgpt-data-security\"\u003esecuring data in ChatGPT\u003c/a\u003e, Forcepoint DSPM can see data being shared with the chatbot in real time and can revoke that data from the application.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/dlp-data-loss-prevention\"\u003eForcepoint Data Loss Prevention\u003c/a\u003e helps organizations create, manage and enforce policies designed to prevent sensitive information such as PII, PHI and other types of regulated or proprietary data from being shared with AI. These policies deliver unparalleled control by blocking the copying and pasting of data into GenAI to stop risky activity with shadow AI in real time.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLastly, \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eForcepoint Cloud Access Security Broker\u003c/a\u003e (CASB) and \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-web-security\"\u003eForcepoint Secure Web Gateway\u003c/a\u003e (SWG) can be used in tandem to control access to AI applications on the cloud and web. When it comes to \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/use-case/chatgpt-data-security\"\u003esecuring data in ChatGPT\u003c/a\u003e, Forcepoint DSPM can see data being shared with the chatbot in real time and can revoke that data from the application.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/dlp-data-loss-prevention\"\u003eForcepoint Data Loss Prevention\u003c/a\u003e helps organizations create, manage and enforce policies designed to prevent sensitive information such as PII, PHI and other types of regulated or proprietary data from being shared with AI. These policies deliver unparalleled control by blocking the copying and pasting of data into GenAI to stop risky activity with shadow AI in real time.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLastly, \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eForcepoint Cloud Access Security Broker\u003c/a\u003e (CASB) and \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-web-security\"\u003eForcepoint Secure Web Gateway\u003c/a\u003e (SWG) can be used in tandem to control access to AI applications on the cloud and web. It can limit access based on factors such as the user’s position or team, and direct employees to approved software where there is overlap—from Gemini to ChatGPT for example.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/form/demo-request\"\u003eTalk to an expert\u003c/a\u003e today to explore all the ways Forcepoint can deliver visibility and control over shadow AI to keep your organization’s data safe.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","format":"full_html"},"pgBackgroundImage":null,"paragraphClasses":null,"paragraphFullWidth":false}],"metatag":[{"__typename":"MetaTagValue","tag":"meta","attributes":{"content":"How to Get Visibility and Control of Shadow AI- Forcepoint","name":"title"}},{"__typename":"MetaTagValue","tag":"meta","attributes":{"content":"Popular chatbots and AI-powered everything have given way to shadow AI— the unapproved corporate use of GenAI tools and AI software. Lionel: \u003c/strong\u003eWelcome to the fourth and final post in our Future Insights 2025 series. In this post, Field CTO \u0026amp; Director of Strategic Business, APAC \u003ca href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/savvidesnick/?originalSubdomain=au\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNick Savvides\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/a\u003e tackles privacy regulation and the forces that will impact it looking ahead. \u003ca style=\"--tw-backdrop-blur:;--tw-backdrop-brightness:;--tw-backdrop-contrast:;--tw-backdrop-grayscale:;--tw-backdrop-hue-rotate:;--tw-backdrop-invert:;--tw-backdrop-opacity:;--tw-backdrop-saturate:;--tw-backdrop-sepia:;--tw-blur:;--tw-border-spacing-x:0;--tw-border-spacing-y:0;--tw-brightness:;--tw-contrast:;--tw-drop-shadow:;--tw-gradient-from-position:;--tw-gradient-to-position:;--tw-gradient-via-position:;--tw-grayscale:;--tw-hue-rotate:;--tw-invert:;--tw-numeric-figure:;--tw-numeric-fraction:;--tw-numeric-spacing:;--tw-ordinal:;--tw-pan-x:;--tw-pan-y:;--tw-pinch-zoom:;--tw-ring-color:rgba(59,130,246,.5);--tw-ring-inset:;--tw-ring-offset-color:#fff;--tw-ring-offset-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-ring-offset-width:0px;--tw-ring-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-rotate:0;--tw-saturate:;--tw-scale-x:1;--tw-scale-y:1;--tw-scroll-snap-strictness:proximity;--tw-sepia:;--tw-shadow-colored:0 0 #0000;--tw-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-skew-x:0;--tw-skew-y:0;--tw-slashed-zero:;--tw-text-opacity:1;--tw-translate-x:0;--tw-translate-y:0;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;box-sizing:border-box;color:rgb(0 117 101/var(--tw-text-opacity));font-weight:500;text-decoration:underline;\" href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/tags/future-insights-2025\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eClick to read previous posts\u003c/a\u003e in the series.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"\" style=\"--tw-backdrop-blur:;--tw-backdrop-brightness:;--tw-backdrop-contrast:;--tw-backdrop-grayscale:;--tw-backdrop-hue-rotate:;--tw-backdrop-invert:;--tw-backdrop-opacity:;--tw-backdrop-saturate:;--tw-backdrop-sepia:;--tw-blur:;--tw-border-spacing-x:0;--tw-border-spacing-y:0;--tw-brightness:;--tw-contrast:;--tw-drop-shadow:;--tw-gradient-from-position:;--tw-gradient-to-position:;--tw-gradient-via-position:;--tw-grayscale:;--tw-hue-rotate:;--tw-invert:;--tw-numeric-figure:;--tw-numeric-fraction:;--tw-numeric-spacing:;--tw-ordinal:;--tw-pan-x:;--tw-pan-y:;--tw-pinch-zoom:;--tw-ring-color:rgba(59,130,246,.5);--tw-ring-inset:;--tw-ring-offset-color:#fff;--tw-ring-offset-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-ring-offset-width:0px;--tw-ring-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-rotate:0;--tw-saturate:;--tw-scale-x:1;--tw-scale-y:1;--tw-scroll-snap-strictness:proximity;--tw-sepia:;--tw-shadow-colored:0 0 #0000;--tw-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-skew-x:0;--tw-skew-y:0;--tw-slashed-zero:;--tw-text-opacity:1;--tw-translate-x:0;--tw-translate-y:0;-webkit-text-stroke-width:0px;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;box-sizing:border-box;color:rgb(83 87 90/var(--tw-text-opacity));font-family:__hovesFont_51a801, __hovesFont_Fallback_51a801, sans-serif;font-size:16px;font-style:normal;font-variant-caps:normal;font-variant-ligatures:normal;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:-0.1px;line-height:22.4px;margin:1.25em 0px;orphans:2;text-align:start;text-decoration-color:initial;text-decoration-style:initial;text-decoration-thickness:initial;text-indent:0px;text-transform:none;white-space:normal;widows:2;word-spacing:0px;\"\u003e###\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eTwo years ago, I gave the first in a series of forward-looking talks examining the impact of geopolitics and demographics on the global cybersecurity landscape. One of my key predictions was that a more multilateral world order was coming into being, with significant ramifications for cybersecurity. From consuming technologies to building them; from hiring cyber-warriors to implementing AI automation; from financing start-ups to complying with regulation—all of this would become significantly harder, more complex and more expensive.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eHere I’m going to take a closer look at one part of this big picture: Namely, how the balkanization of global privacy regulation will impact data security. I see AI adoption accelerating this trend, leading to major developments and challenges in 2025.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAn old trend, picking up speed\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003ePrivacy regulations are not new, having been around in one form or another for decades. We’ve had regulations at the national, sub-national and super-national levels, all covering different and overlapping areas.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis has always been a complex area, but the internet era enhanced this complexity as regulators all scrambled to modernize. We saw significant changes and the introduction of new laws in every major jurisdiction throughout the 1990s and 2000s. In some jurisdictions, we even had competing regulations, typically around collection and retention, where complying with one meant you were not compliant with another.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eBy the mid-2010s, companies struggled to maintain compliance with the myriad of rules, and things would get even more complicated with the extra-jurisdictional implications of the European General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR), which expanded regulatory capture to anyone processing EU citizen information.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eFor some time there appeared to be concerted efforts to streamline regulations, aiming not necessarily at harmonization but rather at mutual recognition. This was based on how cross-recognition has helped other highly-regulated areas, such as telecommunications, electronics and aircraft and automotive manufacturing.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eIt is well understood that over-regulation has a significant negative impact on economic growth and innovation. Regulators in all fields look to strike a balance between regulation and innovation. Unfortunately, it is the nature of rules that they constantly grow. It takes major shakeups and real effort to streamline and optimize them, and for a while I was hopeful this would happen here.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eBut presently there is a nexus of forces working against this, all against a backdrop of businesses collecting, processing and storing more data than ever but also now feeding their data-hungry AI models.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eRegulatory expansion and balkanization\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI no longer think we should hold out too much hope when it comes to streamlining regulation. One major reason for this is the geopolitical shift to a multilateral world order.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eMy prediction here is that we will see some streamlining, but it will be in clusters, aligned with geopolitical groupings of countries. When I say this, I usually get asked, “But isn’t that still good, if it reduces the burden of compliance?” The big issue is that I believe there will be enforced lack of cross-recognition and intentional introduction of differences between the clusters. Friction and complexity will be by design.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI also believe we will see significantly conflicting regulation, where what is obligated in one jurisdiction is explicitly prohibited in another. For example, companies might be forced to collect some information in one jurisdiction but prohibited from collecting it at all in another. Some collected information may be allowed for some purposes in one jurisdiction but prohibited for those same purposes in another.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eCompanies operating across these market jurisdictions are going to need to know what their obligations are, to which regulators, to which users, to which data, where that data is stored, how this data is being used downstream and how this data is managed throughout its lifecycle.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAll of this sounds expensive and complicated, because it is. It will likely result in duplicated infrastructure and services, bigger compliance problems, significant residual risk and a myriad of policies and procedures operating inside organizations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThe AI revolution\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis wouldn’t be a contemporary discussion if we didn’t discuss AI. We have businesses scrambling to use it, and governments scrambling to regulate it. AI has captured the imagination not just of creators, but of regulators as well.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe are still very early in the era of generative AI and of outsourcing decision-making to AI, but regulators are moving quickly. We have already seen significant new regulation and proposed regulation around AI. Unfortunately for innovation, we are also seeing regulation in some jurisdictions that ranges from mildly excessive to cripplingly onerous.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eA few weeks ago, I was invited to contribute to a panel at GovWare discussing data security considerations when adopting AI. Now, GovWare is the biggest cybersecurity conference in Asia-Pacific, with over 13,000 attendees. It’s probably superfluous to say, but the massive show floor was absolutely covered with the letters “AI.” Even with all of that, I still don’t think we’ve hit peak AI hype.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThe panel was on the second day of the conference, and the attendees had already been inundated with AI content and messaging. You’d think the audience would be tired of the topic, but they couldn’t get enough. After a wide-ranging conversation, we were bombarded with questions, not about AI technology, but rather about governance and security, with a real focus on how to manage all the data that AI demands.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAnd here is what leads us to the multilateral problem. Vast volumes of data are required for AI to be effective, productive and generative.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis is a problem when this data is covered not just by balkanized and conflicting data privacy regulations, but also AI regulations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe are facing the prospect of organizations only being able to use AI with data collected in certain jurisdictions. Derivative works—the generative output—and business outcomes may have be different in different jurisdictions. Commingled data that may be acceptable for a human to access may not be allowed for AI.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eEven worse, what happens to models based on data, where permission for use by AI \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/impact-of-legislation-on-ai\"\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003ecan be revoked\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e by the data subject at any time?\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThese are not just design-time considerations; these are operational, ongoing considerations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAI has become a proxy for geopolitical strategic goals, and I expect that the current challenges around access to semiconductors, AI tools and software are going to spill over into the data protection environment.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe can’t give up on data privacy regulation\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAfter reading all of that, it’s easy to say that we will all just struggle along: Some will get breached, some will violate laws, some will receive massive fines and some will spend years in court. And while there is a little bit of truth to this, there are things we can do to be prepared.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eA rubric that has served me well in this area has been to ask and answer two questions:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e“Am I a good custodian of the data that I hold?”\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e“Am I doing what is expected of me to protect data?”\u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThese questions are still very valuable today, even in a multilateral world. Typically, on an individual regulator level, when something goes wrong, reasonable regulators and authorities will measure you against these questions and use them to determine follow-up actions.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI deliberately chose the word custodian because so much follows from it. To be a good custodian you must know what data you hold, where it is, what it’s regulated by and who has access to it. From protection follows observability and controls of data usage.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis is a good start, but the multilateral order demands that we also prioritize efficiency. This may come as a surprise with so many other considerations to choose from, but I believe efficiency will make or break everything else.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eOrganizations must embrace technologies that will allow them to scale their data security and privacy practices to cover this new complex environment. If this doesn’t happen, the programs will collapse to deal with their core jurisdictions, and the others will fall by the wayside. In the past this might have been unfortunate, but now it could be catastrophic.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eFrom efficiency flows tooling, empowering end-user employees to quickly identify what regulations apply to the data they are using. This must be paired with revamped education programs to elevate users’ understanding and management of data.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWhile some may disagree with my thesis here, I think we can all agree that data security, privacy and regulation problems are only going to get bigger and more challenging. It is our task to identify and implement solutions that will keep these problems from spiralling out of control.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","processed":"\u003cp Lionel: \u003c/strong\u003eWelcome to the fourth and final post in our Future Insights 2025 series. In this post, Field CTO \u0026amp; Director of Strategic Business, APAC \u003ca href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/savvidesnick/?originalSubdomain=au\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNick Savvides\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/a\u003e tackles privacy regulation and the forces that will impact it looking ahead. \u003ca style=\"--tw-backdrop-blur:;--tw-backdrop-brightness:;--tw-backdrop-contrast:;--tw-backdrop-grayscale:;--tw-backdrop-hue-rotate:;--tw-backdrop-invert:;--tw-backdrop-opacity:;--tw-backdrop-saturate:;--tw-backdrop-sepia:;--tw-blur:;--tw-border-spacing-x:0;--tw-border-spacing-y:0;--tw-brightness:;--tw-contrast:;--tw-drop-shadow:;--tw-gradient-from-position:;--tw-gradient-to-position:;--tw-gradient-via-position:;--tw-grayscale:;--tw-hue-rotate:;--tw-invert:;--tw-numeric-figure:;--tw-numeric-fraction:;--tw-numeric-spacing:;--tw-ordinal:;--tw-pan-x:;--tw-pan-y:;--tw-pinch-zoom:;--tw-ring-color:rgba(59,130,246,.5);--tw-ring-inset:;--tw-ring-offset-color:#fff;--tw-ring-offset-shadow:0 #0000;--tw-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-skew-x:0;--tw-skew-y:0;--tw-slashed-zero:;--tw-text-opacity:1;--tw-translate-x:0;--tw-translate-y:0;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;box-sizing:border-box;color:rgb(0 117 101/var(--tw-text-opacity));font-weight:500;text-decoration:underline;\" href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/tags/future-insights-2025\" target=\"_blank\"\u003eClick to read previous posts\u003c/a\u003e in the series.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class style=\"--tw-backdrop-blur:;--tw-backdrop-brightness:;--tw-backdrop-contrast:;--tw-backdrop-grayscale:;--tw-backdrop-hue-rotate:;--tw-backdrop-invert:;--tw-backdrop-opacity:;--tw-backdrop-saturate:;--tw-backdrop-sepia:;--tw-blur:;--tw-border-spacing-x:0;--tw-border-spacing-y:0;--tw-brightness:;--tw-contrast:;--tw-drop-shadow:;--tw-gradient-from-position:;--tw-gradient-to-position:;--tw-gradient-via-position:;--tw-grayscale:;--tw-hue-rotate:;--tw-invert:;--tw-numeric-figure:;--tw-numeric-fraction:;--tw-numeric-spacing:;--tw-ordinal:;--tw-pan-x:;--tw-pan-y:;--tw-pinch-zoom:;--tw-ring-color:rgba(59,130,246,.5);--tw-ring-inset:;--tw-ring-offset-color:#fff;--tw-ring-offset-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-ring-offset-width:0px;--tw-ring-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-rotate:0;--tw-saturate:;--tw-scale-x:1;--tw-scale-y:1;--tw-scroll-snap-strictness:proximity;--tw-sepia:;--tw-shadow-colored:0 0 #0000;--tw-shadow:0 0 #0000;--tw-skew-x:0;--tw-skew-y:0;--tw-slashed-zero:;--tw-text-opacity:1;--tw-translate-x:0;--tw-translate-y:0;-webkit-text-stroke-width:0px;border-style:solid;border-width:0px;box-sizing:border-box;color:rgb(83 87 90/var(--tw-text-opacity));font-family:__hovesFont_51a801, __hovesFont_Fallback_51a801, sans-serif;font-size:16px;font-style:normal;font-variant-caps:normal;font-variant-ligatures:normal;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:-0.1px;line-height:22.4px;margin:1.25em 0px;orphans:2;text-align:start;text-decoration-color:initial;text-decoration-style:initial;text-decoration-thickness:initial;text-indent:0px;text-transform:none;white-space:normal;widows:2;word-spacing:0px;\"\u003e###\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eTwo years ago, I gave the first in a series of forward-looking talks examining the impact of geopolitics and demographics on the global cybersecurity landscape. One of my key predictions was that a more multilateral world order was coming into being, with significant ramifications for cybersecurity. From consuming technologies to building them; from hiring cyber-warriors to implementing AI automation; from financing start-ups to complying with regulation—all of this would become significantly harder, more complex and more expensive.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eHere I’m going to take a closer look at one part of this big picture: Namely, how the balkanization of global privacy regulation will impact data security. I see AI adoption accelerating this trend, leading to major developments and challenges in 2025.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAn old trend, picking up speed\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003ePrivacy regulations are not new, having been around in one form or another for decades. We’ve had regulations at the national, sub-national and super-national levels, all covering different and overlapping areas.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis has always been a complex area, but the internet era enhanced this complexity as regulators all scrambled to modernize. We saw significant changes and the introduction of new laws in every major jurisdiction throughout the 1990s and 2000s. In some jurisdictions, we even had competing regulations, typically around collection and retention, where complying with one meant you were not compliant with another.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eBy the mid-2010s, companies struggled to maintain compliance with the myriad of rules, and things would get even more complicated with the extra-jurisdictional implications of the European General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR), which expanded regulatory capture to anyone processing EU citizen information.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eFor some time there appeared to be concerted efforts to streamline regulations, aiming not necessarily at harmonization but rather at mutual recognition. This was based on how cross-recognition has helped other highly-regulated areas, such as telecommunications, electronics and aircraft and automotive manufacturing.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eIt is well understood that over-regulation has a significant negative impact on economic growth and innovation. Regulators in all fields look to strike a balance between regulation and innovation. Unfortunately, it is the nature of rules that they constantly grow. It takes major shakeups and real effort to streamline and optimize them, and for a while I was hopeful this would happen here.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eBut presently there is a nexus of forces working against this, all against a backdrop of businesses collecting, processing and storing more data than ever but also now feeding their data-hungry AI models.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eRegulatory expansion and balkanization\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI no longer think we should hold out too much hope when it comes to streamlining regulation. One major reason for this is the geopolitical shift to a multilateral world order.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eMy prediction here is that we will see some streamlining, but it will be in clusters, aligned with geopolitical groupings of countries. When I say this, I usually get asked, “But isn’t that still good, if it reduces the burden of compliance?” The big issue is that I believe there will be enforced lack of cross-recognition and intentional introduction of differences between the clusters. Friction and complexity will be by design.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI also believe we will see significantly conflicting regulation, where what is obligated in one jurisdiction is explicitly prohibited in another. For example, companies might be forced to collect some information in one jurisdiction but prohibited from collecting it at all in another. Some collected information may be allowed for some purposes in one jurisdiction but prohibited for those same purposes in another.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eCompanies operating across these market jurisdictions are going to need to know what their obligations are, to which regulators, to which users, to which data, where that data is stored, how this data is being used downstream and how this data is managed throughout its lifecycle.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAll of this sounds expensive and complicated, because it is. It will likely result in duplicated infrastructure and services, bigger compliance problems, significant residual risk and a myriad of policies and procedures operating inside organizations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThe AI revolution\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis wouldn’t be a contemporary discussion if we didn’t discuss AI. We have businesses scrambling to use it, and governments scrambling to regulate it. AI has captured the imagination not just of creators, but of regulators as well.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe are still very early in the era of generative AI and of outsourcing decision-making to AI, but regulators are moving quickly. We have already seen significant new regulation and proposed regulation around AI. Unfortunately for innovation, we are also seeing regulation in some jurisdictions that ranges from mildly excessive to cripplingly onerous.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eA few weeks ago, I was invited to contribute to a panel at GovWare discussing data security considerations when adopting AI. Now, GovWare is the biggest cybersecurity conference in Asia-Pacific, with over 13,000 attendees. It’s probably superfluous to say, but the massive show floor was absolutely covered with the letters “AI.” Even with all of that, I still don’t think we’ve hit peak AI hype.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThe panel was on the second day of the conference, and the attendees had already been inundated with AI content and messaging. You’d think the audience would be tired of the topic, but they couldn’t get enough. After a wide-ranging conversation, we were bombarded with questions, not about AI technology, but rather about governance and security, with a real focus on how to manage all the data that AI demands.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAnd here is what leads us to the multilateral problem. Vast volumes of data are required for AI to be effective, productive and generative.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis is a problem when this data is covered not just by balkanized and conflicting data privacy regulations, but also AI regulations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe are facing the prospect of organizations only being able to use AI with data collected in certain jurisdictions. Derivative works—the generative output—and business outcomes may have be different in different jurisdictions. Commingled data that may be acceptable for a human to access may not be allowed for AI.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eEven worse, what happens to models based on data, where permission for use by AI \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/impact-of-legislation-on-ai\"\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003ecan be revoked\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e by the data subject at any time?\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThese are not just design-time considerations; these are operational, ongoing considerations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAI has become a proxy for geopolitical strategic goals, and I expect that the current challenges around access to semiconductors, AI tools and software are going to spill over into the data protection environment.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWe can’t give up on data privacy regulation\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eAfter reading all of that, it’s easy to say that we will all just struggle along: Some will get breached, some will violate laws, some will receive massive fines and some will spend years in court. And while there is a little bit of truth to this, there are things we can do to be prepared.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eA rubric that has served me well in this area has been to ask and answer two questions:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e“Am I a good custodian of the data that I hold?”\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003e“Am I doing what is expected of me to protect data?”\u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp; \u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThese questions are still very valuable today, even in a multilateral world. Typically, on an individual regulator level, when something goes wrong, reasonable regulators and authorities will measure you against these questions and use them to determine follow-up actions.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eI deliberately chose the word custodian because so much follows from it. To be a good custodian you must know what data you hold, where it is, what it’s regulated by and who has access to it. From protection follows observability and controls of data usage.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eThis is a good start, but the multilateral order demands that we also prioritize efficiency. This may come as a surprise with so many other considerations to choose from, but I believe efficiency will make or break everything else.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eOrganizations must embrace technologies that will allow them to scale their data security and privacy practices to cover this new complex environment. If this doesn’t happen, the programs will collapse to deal with their core jurisdictions, and the others will fall by the wayside. In the past this might have been unfortunate, but now it could be catastrophic.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eFrom efficiency flows tooling, empowering end-user employees to quickly identify what regulations apply to the data they are using. This must be paired with revamped education programs to elevate users’ understanding and management of data.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan lang=\"EN-AU\"\u003eWhile some may disagree with my thesis here, I think we can all agree that data security, privacy and regulation problems are only going to get bigger and more challenging. It is our task to identify and implement solutions that will keep these problems from spiralling out of control.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","format":"full_html"},"pgBackgroundImage":null,"paragraphClasses":null,"paragraphFullWidth":false}],"metatag":[{"__typename":"MetaTagValue","tag":"meta","attributes":{"content":"The from Lionel: \u003c/strong\u003eAs our X-Labs team was in the process of final analysis, we noticed the IBM X-Force team \u003ca href=\"https://securityintelligence.com/x-force/strela-stealer-todays-invoice-tomorrows-phish/\"\u003erecently published details\u003c/a\u003e on the Strela Stealer malware. In the interest of sharing more information, we thought it was worth communicating it here via a blog post.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e###\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eIn the last month, we’ve seen a pronounced\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e \u003c/span\u003eincrease in an infostealer malware that has been active throughout 2024. The Strela\u003cspan\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003eStealer malware campaign starts via a German language phishing email that urges users to download an archive that contains highly obfuscated large JavaScript file. Upon execution, this file acts as a stealer that exfiltrates certain system information—including email configuration details, usernames and passwords.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eHere's the attack chain:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media file is around ~1MB. The JavaScript has two techniques for execution of code:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003eBy using \u003cstrong\u003ecmd.exe\u0026nbsp;\u003c/strong\u003ewhich directly executing a dll file using rundll32\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eBy using \u003cstrong\u003epowershell.exe\u003c/strong\u003e, de-obfuscating base64 encoded string and executing a dll file using rundll32\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eHere’s more detail in how the de-obfuscation and execution techniques work:\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eTechnique1: Obfuscated JavaScript and execution using cmd.exe\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"2590281d-abc6-4e33-8cb0-f7eb602a298a\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 3 - JavaScript code\u0026amp;nbsp;\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eObserving the JavaScript, we see it has two parts. This dll acts as a wrapper for the malware payload.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"a3b08f6d-1de9-47a8-b9d1-864f79d1c946\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 5 – DLL export function\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eOn static analysis, we found .text and .data sections are packed which seems to be containing encrypted code.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"33eb7674-c094-4656-baa8-ae7399c38781\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 6 - \u0026amp;nbsp;File sections\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eOn checking the data section, we see the encryption key highlighted below:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"984b4d42-2d7c-40e9-a13c-fe556342c217\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 7 – Packed data section shows encrypted string\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe dll file also contains numerous jump functions which makes debugging harder to do. \u003cstrong\u003eFig. 8.\u003c/strong\u003e below shows these multiple jump instructions:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"e1a7bfbf-f1f9-4199-b32a-bdf0e8cace4f\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;span style=\u0026quot;font-family:\u0026amp;quot;Aptos\u0026amp;quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;\u0026quot;\u0026gt;\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 8 - Multiple jump instructions\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/span\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eUpon executing the dll till return, it follows certain XOR and arithmetic operation for decryption of MZ DOS content inside the dll file:\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"9d35e36c-fbd1-40f6-9767-54bfaf32d5ef\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 9 - Encryption key\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 10\u003c/strong\u003e below shows encryption key which is used to decrypt additional MZ header. This encoded string is similar to what we saw in the static analysis of the dll file in \u003cstrong\u003eFig. 7 \u003c/strong\u003eearlier.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"28a09132-c4d8-4240-9d16-2b66cb69a6b0\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 10 - Fake error message\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\u0026lt;o:p\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/o:p\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePresence of PE file\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cdrupal-media data-entity-type=\"media\" data-entity-uuid=\"d6071bd7-18af-4875-85dc-df5c7bf05da1\" data-caption=\"\u0026lt;strong\u0026gt;Fig. 11 - Presence of PE file\u0026lt;/strong\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/drupal-media\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eUpon successful execution the dll file exits by displaying a fake error message (See Fig. 10) while remaining active in the background. It then directly executes—unpacking the payload using \u003cstrong\u003erundll32\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eWhile the file is running in background, it tries to get local settings from the victim’s machine by utilizing the \u003cstrong\u003eGetKeyboardLayout API\u003c/strong\u003e. It then checks and compares for hardcoded languages such as German and Spanish. If languages match the\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e \u003c/span\u003evictim’s system, it then continues execution, exfiltrating sensitive system data on /server[.]php.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eConclusion:\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe recent Strela infostealer campaign is distributed by phishing email that urges users to download an infected file attached to the email. The file archive contains heavily obfuscated JavaScript code which uses WebDAV server to directly execute the dll file without saving it to disk—thus bypassing security mechanisms, enabling unauthorized access to sensitive information in the process.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eProtection Statement\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 2 (Lure)\u003c/strong\u003e – Delivered via archive embedded in an email. Emails are blocked by email analytics.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 3 (Redirect)\u003c/strong\u003e – WebDAV url which hosts dll file is categorized and blocked under security classification.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 5 (Dropper File)\u003c/strong\u003e - The dropper files are added to Forcepoint malicious database and are blocked.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 6 (Call Home)\u003c/strong\u003e - The malware contacts command and control (C\u0026amp;C) servers in order to share sensitive user data are categorized and blocked under security classification.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003eIOCs\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ctable style=\"border-collapse:collapse;\" border=\"1\" cellspacing=\"0\" Decoded command\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 4.4\u003c/strong\u003e and \u003cstrong\u003e4.7\u003c/strong\u003e above both show decoded code that uses WebDAV to run a file without saving it to disk.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eWebDAV server enhances HTTP and allows users to manage and edit files on server without saving changes on the local machine.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe code connects to 94.159.113[.]82 using \u003cstrong\u003eport 8888\u003c/strong\u003e to execute the dll file using \u003cstrong\u003erundll32.exe \u003c/strong\u003eon server.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAnalysis of dll file\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe dll file which is present on WebDAV server is 64-bit dll file that contains one export function named Entry. This dll acts as a wrapper for the malware payload.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-13.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"189\" alt=\"strela_image-13.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 5 – DLL export function\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eOn static analysis, we found .text and .data sections are packed which seems to be containing encrypted code.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-14.png\" width=\"562\" height=\"136\" alt=\"strela_image-14.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 6 - \u0026nbsp;File sections\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eOn checking the data section, we see the encryption key highlighted below:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-15.png\" width=\"409\" height=\"306\" alt=\"strela_image-15.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 7 – Packed data section shows encrypted string\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe dll file also contains numerous jump functions which makes debugging harder to do. \u003cstrong\u003eFig. 8.\u003c/strong\u003e below shows these multiple jump instructions:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-16.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"631\" alt=\"strela_image-16.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 8 - Multiple jump instructions\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eUpon executing the dll till return, it follows certain XOR and arithmetic operation for decryption of MZ DOS content inside the dll file:\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-17.png\" width=\"630\" height=\"220\" alt=\"strela_image-17.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 9 - Encryption key\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 10\u003c/strong\u003e below shows encryption key which is used to decrypt additional MZ header. This encoded string is similar to what we saw in the static analysis of the dll file in \u003cstrong\u003eFig. 7 \u003c/strong\u003eearlier.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-18.png\" width=\"613\" height=\"401\" alt=\"strela_image-18.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 10 - Fake error message\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePresence of PE file\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure role=\"group\" class=\"caption caption-drupal-media\"\u003e\n\u003carticle class=\"media media--type-image media--view-mode-full-size\"\u003e\n  \n      \n  \u003cdiv class=\"field field--name-field-media-image field--type-image field--label-visually_hidden\"\u003e\n    \u003cdiv class=\"field__label visually-hidden\"\u003eImage\u003c/div\u003e\n              \u003cdiv class=\"field__item\"\u003e  \u003cimg src=\"/sites/default/files/2024-11/strela_image-19.png\" width=\"614\" height=\"320\" alt=\"strela_image-19.png\" loading=\"lazy\"\u003e\n\n\u003c/div\u003e\n          \u003c/div\u003e\n\n  \u003c/article\u003e\n\n\u003cfigcaption\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFig. 11 - Presence of PE file\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/figcaption\u003e\n\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eUpon successful execution the dll file exits by displaying a fake error message (See Fig. 10) while remaining active in the background. It then directly executes—unpacking the payload using \u003cstrong\u003erundll32\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eWhile the file is running in background, it tries to get local settings from the victim’s machine by utilizing the \u003cstrong\u003eGetKeyboardLayout API\u003c/strong\u003e. It then checks and compares for hardcoded languages such as German and Spanish. If languages match the\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e \u003c/span\u003evictim’s system, it then continues execution, exfiltrating sensitive system data on /server[.]php.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eConclusion:\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eThe recent Strela infostealer campaign is distributed by phishing email that urges users to download an infected file attached to the email. The file archive contains heavily obfuscated JavaScript code which uses WebDAV server to directly execute the dll file without saving it to disk—thus bypassing security mechanisms, enabling unauthorized access to sensitive information in the process.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eProtection Statement\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 2 (Lure)\u003c/strong\u003e – Delivered via archive embedded in an email. Emails are blocked by email analytics.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 3 (Redirect)\u003c/strong\u003e – WebDAV url which hosts dll file is categorized and blocked under security classification.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 5 (Dropper File)\u003c/strong\u003e - The dropper files are added to Forcepoint malicious database and are blocked.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStage 6 (Call Home)\u003c/strong\u003e - The malware contacts command and control (C\u0026amp;C) servers in order to share sensitive user data are categorized and blocked under security classification.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003eIOCs\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ctable style=\"border-collapse:collapse;\" border=\"1\" cellspacing=\"0\"
