security best practices provide a framework for protecting data assets, helping organizations to minimize vulnerabilities and ensure data integrity, confidentiality and availability.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eStart Broad with Information Security Best Practices\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe foundation of effective information security lies in adopting a multi-layered approach. From implementing robust access controls and encryption measures to conducting regular employee training, each layer plays a unique role in defending against potential threats.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese best practices not only reduce the risk of data breaches but also enable organizations to comply with regulatory requirements, while helping to build trust with clients and stakeholders.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e1. Implement Strong Access Controls:\u003c/strong\u003e Effective access control is at the core of information security. It requires a robust framework that limits access to sensitive information based on user roles and responsibilities. Regular audits of access logs and permissions ensures only authorized employees have access to critical data, minimizing the risk of insider threats and unauthorized access.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e2. Regularly Update and Patch Systems:\u003c/strong\u003e Cyber attackers often exploit weaknesses in outdated software, making regular patch management crucial. Automated patch management tools can streamline this process, ensuring that updates are applied promptly and reducing the likelihood of human error. Maintaining an inventory of all IT assets and their update statuses helps manage vulnerabilities effectively and ensures comprehensive protection.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e3. Conduct Security Audits and Penetration Testing:\u003c/strong\u003e Regular security audits and penetration testing are proactive measures to identify and address vulnerabilities in IT infrastructure. Security audits involve a thorough review of systems, policies and procedures to ensure compliance with security standards. Penetration testing simulates cyberattacks to find and fix weaknesses before malicious actors can exploit them. These assessments provide valuable insights into the effectiveness of security measures and help in continuously improving defenses.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e4. Educate and Train Employees:\u003c/strong\u003e Human error is often the weakest link in the security chain. Ongoing education and training programs are vital in fostering a security-conscious culture within organizations. Engaging training sessions with practical examples and simulations help ensure that employees understand and can apply security protocols effectively.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eZero in with Information Technology Security Best Practices\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhile securing information is key, it’s also important to strengthen the technological infrastructure that processes and transmits data. As cyber threats become increasingly sophisticated, information technology security must evolve to protect systems and networks that form the backbone of an organization's digital environment.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy focusing on core information technology security practices, organizations can build a resilient defense against potential breaches and maintain the integrity of their technology landscape. Here are the top IT security best practices that can help achieve this goal.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e1. Network Security:\u003c/strong\u003e Protecting network infrastructure is a fundamental aspect of IT security. Doing it effectively involves implementing multiple layers of defense, including firewalls and network segmentation. Forcepoint’s \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/secure-sd-wan?slug=flexedge-secure-sd-wan\"\u003eSecure SD-WAN\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/ngfw-next-generation-firewall\"\u003eNGFW solutions\u003c/a\u003e monitor and control incoming and outgoing network traffic, acting as a barrier between trusted internal networks and untrusted external networks. Network segmentation divides the network into smaller, isolated segments, limiting the spread of malware and restricting access to sensitive data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e2. Cloud Access Security Broker (CASB):\u003c/strong\u003e Tools like \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eForcepoint CASB\u003c/a\u003e act as intermediaries between enterprise users and cloud service providers, enforcing security policies for cloud application access and usage. Besides access, they also provide visibility, data control and analytics to identify and combat threats. CASBs help manage shadow IT, enforce granular cloud usage controls and provide risk visibility to assess the risk of unsanctioned applications. By leveraging CASBs, organizations can secure their cloud environments and ensure that only authorized users have access to sensitive data and applications.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e3. Data Loss Prevention (DLP):\u003c/strong\u003e Forcepoint’s \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-data-security\"\u003eaward-winning DLP\u003c/a\u003e prevents unauthorized sharing, transfer or use of sensitive data. It monitors and protects sensitive information across on-premises systems, cloud-based locations and endpoint devices. DLP policies can identify, monitor and automatically protect sensitive items by applying protective actions like encryption, access restrictions and more. And tools like \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/risk-adaptive-protection\"\u003eForcepoint’s Risk-Adaptive Protection\u003c/a\u003e goes beyond DLP capabilities to allow organizations to gain meaningful real-time visibility into how users are interacting with the data they access—making it much easier to identify risky behaviors as they happen.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese best practices serve as a starting point to help\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e \u003c/span\u003esecurity professionals create a robust defense against cyber threats and to protect their organization's critical assets. Information security is a dynamic field that requires continuous adaptation to mitigate evolving threats. Staying proactive and vigilant in implementing and updating these measures is key to maintaining a secure digital environment.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","processed":"\u003cp\u003eInformation security best practices provide a framework for protecting data assets, helping organizations to minimize vulnerabilities and ensure data integrity, confidentiality and availability.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eStart Broad with Information Security Best Practices\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe foundation of effective information security lies in adopting a multi-layered approach. has the potential to improve security, optimize cloud application access and performance and simplify network management. However, the potential benefits of SD-WAN extend far beyond its technical capabilities. They include:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003eCost savings\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eFaster application performance\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eImproved network security\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eEnhanced scalability\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eReliable connectivity and uptime\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eIncreased network visibility\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eFaster deployment\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eSimplified network management\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eBetter user experience\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;line-height:106%;\"\u003eNow, let’s dig into each in a bit more detail:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCost savings\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eSD-WAN allows businesses to use a combination of lower-cost internet services such as broadband, instead of relying solely on expensive private connections, like MPLS circuits. By utilizing SD-WAN to supplement and even replace MPLS links, organizations with dispersed offices and locations can considerably reduce their overall WAN costs.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eFaster application performance\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eApplication performance is paramount in today’s business environment, where video conferencing and SaaS applications are critical for productivity. SD-WAN prioritizes traffic based on application’s importance, ensuring that critical applications such as VoIP and video conferencing receive priority and bandwidth they need. This reduces latency, increases performance and enhances the user experience.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#0F4761;font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:106%;\"\u003eImproved network security\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eSD-WAN integrates advanced security features, including Next-Gen firewall, IPS, and secure VPNs, providing end-to-end protection. It automatically detects and reduces threats, ensuring secure and encrypted data transfer across all branches and remote locations.\u003cspan style=\"color:#0F4761;font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:106%;\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#0F4761;font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:106%;\"\u003eEnhanced scalability\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eFor organizations looking to grow and expand their footprint, SD-WAN provides an easy and efficient way to scale their networks. Whether expanding into new markets or opening a new location across town, traditional WAN setups require significant IT resources and time to provision new circuits and equipment. SD-WAN simplifies this process by allowing new sites to be added seamlessly through software-defined deployment and configurations.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eReliable connectivity and uptime\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eBy leveraging SD-WAN intelligent path selection and dynamic failover, organization gain continuous, high-performance connectivity. It optimizes traffic routing to the best available link, minimizing downtime and delivering reliable service, even during network disruptions.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eIncreased network visibility\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eBranch offices are where most business transactions occur. SD-WAN provides centralized monitoring to deliver real-time insights into network health and application performance, helping to identify and address issues more effectively. Additionally, SD-WAN enables administrators to enforce security policies, adjust bandwidth allocation and optimize traffic— all in real time.\u003cstrong\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eFaster deployment\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eCompared to traditional solutions which often involve long setup times and complex configurations, SD-WAN enables substantially faster deployment. Network administrators can deploy, manage, and maintain their SD-WAN through a centralized console, significantly reducing the time and effort necessary to configure and maintain the network. This simplified management allows organizations to be more responsive to business needs.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#0F4761;font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos Display\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:16.0pt;line-height:106%;\"\u003eSimplified network management\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-left:.5in;\"\u003eWith Centralized management, SD-WAN streamlines network administration. Security Service Edge (SSE) capabilities like \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-web-security\"\u003eSecure Web Gateway (SWG)\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eCloud Access Security Brokers (CASB)\u003c/a\u003e provide essential guardrails for distributed workforces, keeping data safeguarded in the cloud and empowering users to securely access what they need on the Web.\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eA CASB will provide visibility and control over data and user activities across cloud services – enforcing security policies, detecting unauthorized access and preventing breaches. Leveraging this in tandem with a SWG provides strengthens defenses for users adopting technologies like GenAI, protecting against potentially malicious websites and activities.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTHREE - Introduce DSPM for visibility \u0026amp; remediation\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eFor digital-first organizations, prioritizing data security everywhere is a no-brainer. Leveraging the proactive power of \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/data-security-posture-management-dspm\"\u003eData Security Posture Management (DSPM)\u003c/a\u003e can help security leaders see how data is stored, used and moved across an organization – raising flags when needed by proactively identifying data risks and empowering decision-making.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eForcepoint DSPM takes this a step further by leveraging AI Mesh technology beyond data discovery to automate security actions and controls using sophisticated workflow orchestration with automated remediation – preventing inappropriate usage and stopping breaches before they occur.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFOUR - Build a security-aware company culture\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eLeveraging the right data security technologies is one part of the equation – the other part is ensuring buy-in from employees and stakeholders by prioritizing employee education. As the threat landscape continues to evolve and expand with the emergence of new technologies, regular training and awareness programs can help employees understand the top risks facing company data and the importance of following established protocols.\u003cspan\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eDouble-Knot Your Data Breach Prevention Strategy\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp style=\"margin-bottom:0in;\"\u003eA mix of strategy, tools and training goes a long way. Like many things in cybersecurity, building a top-notch data breach prevention strategy takes time. But doing it right is well worth the effort. \u003c/strong\u003eWelcome to the third post in our Future Insights 2025 series. This post from the X-Labs research team analyzes the rise of malware campaigns built on top of legitimate infrastructure services. \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/tags/future-insights-2025\"\u003eClick to read previous posts\u003c/a\u003e in the series.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e###\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;\"\u003eThroughout 2024, as we continued tracking activity around the latest malware and phishing campaigns, the X-Labs team noticed a trend: hackers are moving away from using compromised websites for hosting malware to building malware campaigns on legitimate infrastructure services. Based on our data, we expect that trend to accelerate into 2025 and beyond.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMalware Campaign Examples\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTake blogspot.com, Google’s free domain service that provides a subdomain for Blogger. That’s where we found \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/agent-tesla-malware-attacks-travel-industry\"\u003eAgent Tesla malware\u003c/a\u003e authors hosting stage payloads there.\u0026nbsp;\u003cspan\u003e \u003c/span\u003eIn July, we saw a rash of activity emanating where hackers leveraged Trycloudflare.com and Python to \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/asyncrat-python-trycloudflare-malware\"\u003edeploy AsyncRAT malware\u003c/a\u003e. And the Remcos RAT activity we \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/url-shortener-microsoft-word-remcos-rat-trojan\"\u003eblogged about in June\u003c/a\u003e also leveraged Trycloudflare.com. Hackers used TryCloudflare for \u003ca href=\"https://thehackernews.com/2024/08/cybercriminals-abusing-cloudflare.html\"\u003eXWorm and other malware\u003c/a\u003e campaigns as well. The Snakekeylogger malware campaign used Discord CDN as a public content distribution network to host malicious files.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHackers leveraged Secureserver.net heavily for malware activities as well. That was the origin of a malware campaign \u003ca name=\"_Int_uo8YtT4Y\"\u003ewe blogged about \u003c/a\u003ethat primarily \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/url-shortener-microsoft-word-remcos-rat-trojan\"\u003etargeted financial institutions\u003c/a\u003e in Latin America. Additional malware like Grandoreiro and the NetSupport RAT leveraged Secureserver.net domain as well. To provide a sense of scale, Forcepoint intercepted over 3.7 million suspicious emails that contained Secureserver.net URLs just in the last few months:\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%201%20-embedded-secureserver-urls.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn the case of Remcos and Agent Tesla, we found examples of both using free services to host steganography images or other stage downloads:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003euploaddeimagens.com.br \u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003earchive.org\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eraw.githubusercontent.com\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor data exfiltration and command and control communication, several malware campaigns leveraged the following legitimate services:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eONE - Dynamic DNS Services\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003cbr\u003eHackers use these services to change IP addresses in an effort to evade detection.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003efreeddns.noip.com (servequake.com)\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003efreeddns.dynu.com\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003educkdns.org\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTWO - Telegram Bot API\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eThe Telegram Bot API allows bad actors to build bots to interact with users on the Telegram platform.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eapi.telegram.org/bot\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTHREE - Small File Hosting Services\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eStoring files using well-known free storage services makes it more difficult to track malicious activity.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;\"\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003equ.ax\u003c/span\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003estore2.gofile.io/download\u003c/span\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFOUR - Port forwarding services:\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eStoring files in multiple well-known remote locations makes it more difficult to track ongoing malicious activity.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eply.gg\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eportmap.host\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;\"\u003eTo get a sense of scale on the hackers switching to legitimate services, we analyzed threat activity seen on the top 50 web hosting services. That list featured several of the main players like Windows.net, Wordpress.com, Bluehost, Wix, Google’s Firebase and many others. Here’s the graph that shows web hosting platforms with security risks on subdomain:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%202%20-%20security-risks-subdomains.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eLegitimate Services Used for Phishing Campaigns\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTurning our attention to phishing, we’ve come across phishing campaigns where hackers leverage \u003cstrong\u003evarious Cloudflare services\u003c/strong\u003e: Pages to deploy static webpages, and they take advantage of Workers to deploy serverless code to multiple potential locations around the globe. And bad actors also take advantage of the Cloudflare CDN to speed delivery of SaaS apps anywhere in the world.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe’ve observed significant levels of activity on the Windows.net domain where hackers leverage \u003cstrong\u003eAzure Blob Storage\u003c/strong\u003e to host and serve static web content, files and applications. Attackers take advantage of this by hosting phishing pages, malware, or tech support scams on subdomains like \u003ca href=\"http://web.core.windows.net/\" title=\"http://web.core.windows.net\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eweb.core.windows.net\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e or \u003ca href=\"http://azurewebsites.net/\" title=\"http://azurewebsites.net\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eazurewebsites.net\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. These subdomains make the malicious content appear more credible because they are associated with Microsoft’s trusted infrastructure.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd of course, hackers also rely on \u003cstrong\u003eopen-source services like IPFS\u003c/strong\u003e. Its decentralized nature makes it harder to take down web pages, files or applications since they are spread across multiple servers. Hackers count on the fact that traditional web-hosting takedown methods (like contacting the hosting provider) don’t work effectively with IPFS, as the content is distributed across many nodes.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAttackers use rotating malicious URLs, hosted on platforms like AWS or Azure, to evade detection and blocking.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eHackers Thinking Like Digital Marketers\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor phishing campaigns, attackers will sometimes put on their digital marketing hats. In this regard, they resort to tactics like \u003cstrong\u003eSEO poisoning\u003c/strong\u003e, where they’ll use popular or trending keywords in the content of their malicious websites to trick search engines into ranking them higher. These keywords are often related to current events, popular software or security concerns (e.g., \"free antivirus,\" \"Google Authenticator,\" etc.).\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSpeaking of thinking like digital marketers, hackers also \u003cstrong\u003euse Google Ads\u003c/strong\u003e to promote their wares to unsuspecting victims. We’ve observed scenarios where they impersonate items from Google's product line, such as Google Authenticator, or Google Maps for example. They’ll use Google’s Looker Studio to create fake home pages. On those fake pages, they’ll display images that resemble what you’d expect on the Google search page, to trick users into interacting with the fake page. They’ll use ads to lure users to these fake Google pages.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMalware Categories Trend Heading into 2025\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe compared different malware categories detected via our real-time signatures over the last several months to get a sense for what malware categories will trend in 2025. In the graph below, the number of \u003cstrong\u003emalicious websites\u003c/strong\u003e more than quadrupled from less than 100,000 in Q1 2024 to nearly 500,000 instances at the end of Q3. We expect that trend to continue. \u003cstrong\u003ePhishing and scams\u0026nbsp;\u003c/strong\u003erepresented the second most by volume, growing from about 125,000 instances in Q1 to almost 400,000 by the end of Q3 2024. By comparison, we expect the compromised website category to continue to lag those leading malware categories.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%203-%20attack-type-by-quarter.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","processed":"\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote from Lionel: \u003c/strong\u003eWelcome to the third post in our Future Insights 2025 series. Port forwarding services:\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eStoring files in multiple well-known remote locations makes it more difficult to track ongoing malicious activity.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eply.gg\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:#172B4D;font-family:\u0026quot;Segoe UI\u0026quot;,sans-serif;letter-spacing:-.05pt;\"\u003eportmap.host\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;\"\u003eTo get a sense of scale on the hackers switching to legitimate services, we analyzed threat activity seen on the top 50 web hosting services. That list featured several of the main players like Windows.net, Wordpress.com, Bluehost, Wix, Google’s Firebase and many others. Here’s the graph that shows web hosting platforms with security risks on subdomain:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%202%20-%20security-risks-subdomains.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eLegitimate Services Used for Phishing Campaigns\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTurning our attention to phishing, we’ve come across phishing campaigns where hackers leverage \u003cstrong\u003evarious Cloudflare services\u003c/strong\u003e: Pages to deploy static webpages, and they take advantage of Workers to deploy serverless code to multiple potential locations around the globe. And bad actors also take advantage of the Cloudflare CDN to speed delivery of SaaS apps anywhere in the world.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe’ve observed significant levels of activity on the Windows.net domain where hackers leverage \u003cstrong\u003eAzure Blob Storage\u003c/strong\u003e to host and serve static web content, files and applications. Attackers take advantage of this by hosting phishing pages, malware, or tech support scams on subdomains like \u003ca href=\"http://web.core.windows.net/\" title=\"http://web.core.windows.net\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eweb.core.windows.net\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e or \u003ca href=\"http://azurewebsites.net/\" title=\"http://azurewebsites.net\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eazurewebsites.net\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. These subdomains make the malicious content appear more credible because they are associated with Microsoft’s trusted infrastructure.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd of course, hackers also rely on \u003cstrong\u003eopen-source services like IPFS\u003c/strong\u003e. Its decentralized nature makes it harder to take down web pages, files or applications since they are spread across multiple servers. Hackers count on the fact that traditional web-hosting takedown methods (like contacting the hosting provider) don’t work effectively with IPFS, as the content is distributed across many nodes.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAttackers use rotating malicious URLs, hosted on platforms like AWS or Azure, to evade detection and blocking.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eHackers Thinking Like Digital Marketers\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor phishing campaigns, attackers will sometimes put on their digital marketing hats. In this regard, they resort to tactics like \u003cstrong\u003eSEO poisoning\u003c/strong\u003e, where they’ll use popular or trending keywords in the content of their malicious websites to trick search engines into ranking them higher. These keywords are often related to current events, popular software or security concerns (e.g., \"free antivirus,\" \"Google Authenticator,\" etc.).\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSpeaking of thinking like digital marketers, hackers also \u003cstrong\u003euse Google Ads\u003c/strong\u003e to promote their wares to unsuspecting victims. We’ve observed scenarios where they impersonate items from Google's product line, such as Google Authenticator, or Google Maps for example. They’ll use Google’s Looker Studio to create fake home pages. On those fake pages, they’ll display images that resemble what you’d expect on the Google search page, to trick users into interacting with the fake page. They’ll use ads to lure users to these fake Google pages.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMalware Categories Trend Heading into 2025\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe compared different malware categories detected via our real-time signatures over the last several months to get a sense for what malware categories will trend in 2025. In the graph below, the number of \u003cstrong\u003emalicious websites\u003c/strong\u003e more than quadrupled from less than 100,000 in Q1 2024 to nearly 500,000 instances at the end of Q3. We expect that trend to continue. \u003cstrong\u003ePhishing and scams\u0026nbsp;\u003c/strong\u003erepresented the second most by volume, growing from about 125,000 instances in Q1 to almost 400,000 by the end of Q3 2024. By comparison, we expect the compromised website category to continue to lag those leading malware categories.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%203-%20attack-type-by-quarter.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","format":"full_html"},"pgBackgroundImage":null,"paragraphClasses":null,"paragraphFullWidth":false},{"__typename":"ParagraphWysiwyg","id":"87443","pgFeatureBody":{"value":"\u003cp\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom there, we decided to take a closer look at which sectors are most at risk due to malicious websites, the leading malware category we examined. This graph below highlights the trends of various sectors at risk due to hosting malicious websites. The \u003cstrong\u003eBusiness and Economy\u003c/strong\u003e sector was impacted most by volume over the last year. But we expect the \u003cstrong\u003eFinancial Data and Services\u003c/strong\u003e platform to outpace it since financial services companies continue to be targeted at a higher rate from Q1 to Q3 2024.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%204%20-%20sectors-at-risk-malicious-sites.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLastly, we looked into which sectors were most at risk due to phishing and scams, the second most popular malware category. Not surprisingly the \u003cstrong\u003eBusiness and Economy\u0026nbsp;\u003c/strong\u003esector leads the way as the most at risk, with a trajectory increasing most from Q1 to Q2 2024 and to a lesser extent between Q2 and Q3 2024. \u003cstrong\u003eInformation Technology\u003c/strong\u003e is the second most sector at risk, though it significantly trails the leading category. See the graph below:\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-11/fig%205%20-%20sectors-at-risk-phishing.png\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eHow AI Fits into the Malware Mix\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eJust like most of us, hackers continue to leverage AI in their efforts. They use it to craft components of a campaign—from writing convincing web copy for fake websites to crafting authentic-sounding emails, to creating well-structured phishing attempts via SMS or even sophisticated voice phishing efforts. They can use it to create convincing documents like invoices, job details, or reference items that carry a malware payload. Or they might use chatbots to engage potential victims via real-time conversations, working to trick them into sharing sensitive information. Similarly, LLMs can also be leveraged to generate context-aware responses, replying quickly to a victim who responds to a phishing email for example. In those cases, real-time conversions may go a long way to increase the believability of an attack.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe other reality is that AI makes technology more accessible to a new generation of hackers. With AI’s help, a young person can create many of the elements of a malware campaign using legitimate services as infrastructure to host and deploy all of it. Add it all up, and it seems there’s a good chance script kiddies will make way for malware kiddies or phishing kiddies. Time will tell.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","processed":"\u003cp\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom there, we decided to take a closer look at which sectors are most at risk due to malicious websites, the leading malware category we examined. your company is typical, that number is probably growing rapidly, with demand coming in from all of your business functions. The ease of implementation and the collaborative capabilities that SaaS products offer make them indispensable for most operations. But adopting SaaS tools is only sustainable if you have the right security measures in place to prevent data breaches.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere you’ll find seven SaaS data security best practices to promote safety and productivity for your company. The best practices covered below are:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003eEnforce strong, centralized authentication\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eProactively strengthen your SaaS security posture\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eImplement a Data Loss Prevention (DLP) solution\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eMonitor users with behavioral analytics\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eLeverage AI/ML for advanced capabilities\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUse a CASB to protect SaaS access and discover shadow IT\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUnify control over data security policies\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ch2\u003eEnforce strong, centralized authentication\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eA crucial early step for ensuring SaaS data security is to use robust and consistent authentication mechanisms. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) provides an additional layer of security by requiring users to provide two or more verification factors to gain access.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis significantly reduces the risk of unauthorized access, even if a user’s password is compromised. Identity Access Management (IAM) tools further help by managing user identities and access levels, ensuring that only authorized individuals can access sensitive data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eProactively strengthen your SaaS security posture\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo stay ahead of potential threats, it’s vital to proactively maintain a strong SaaS security posture. This purpose can be accomplished by adopting tools such as \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/data-security-posture-management-dspm\"\u003eData Security Posture Management (DSPM)\u003c/a\u003e – you also may encounter products with broadly overlapping capabilities under category names like Cloud Security Posture Management (CSPM), SaaS Security Posture Management (SSPM) and AI Security Posture Management (AISPM).\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese tools help identify and mitigate security risks by continuously monitoring and assessing your security posture. They provide insights into vulnerabilities and misconfigurations, enabling you to take corrective actions before they can be exploited by attackers.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ch2\u003eImplement a Data Loss Prevention (DLP) solution\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eData Loss Prevention (DLP) solutions are essential for protecting sensitive data from unauthorized access and accidental leaks. A DLP tool monitors and controls data transfers across your network, ensuring that sensitive information is not shared or accessed inappropriately.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy implementing an \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-data-security\"\u003eeffective DLP solution\u003c/a\u003e, you can enforce data security policies, detect potential breaches and prevent data exfiltration. This is particularly important for SaaS products that handle large volumes of sensitive customer data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMonitor users with behavioral analytics\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eUtilizing advanced behavioral analytics makes it possible to automatically monitor user activities and detect anomalous behavior. A tool like \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/risk-adaptive-protection\"\u003eForcepoint Risk-Adaptive Protection\u003c/a\u003e that analyzes behavioral patterns can identify potential security threats such as insider attacks or compromised accounts. This approach allows you to respond to threats in real time, minimizing the risk of data breaches. Implementing Risk-Adaptive Protection as part of your SaaS data security strategy helps ensure that any suspicious activities are quickly flagged and addressed.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eLeverage AI/ML for advanced capabilities\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eArtificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML) provide groundbreaking functionality to enhance SaaS data security, through both automation and improved processes. For instance, the \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/ai-mesh\"\u003eAI Mesh\u003c/a\u003e model employed by Forcepoint DSPM can rapidly and accurately identify sensitive data across your organization, allowing you to eliminate ROT (Redundant, Obsolete or Trivial) data that can easily lead to breaches.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eUse a CASB to protect SaaS access and discover shadow IT\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eCloud Access Security Brokers (CASBs) are essential for protecting access to your SaaS applications. A CASB will provide visibility and control over data and user activities across cloud services. They help enforce security policies, detect unauthorized access and prevent data breaches.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy using a \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eleading CASB\u003c/a\u003e, you can ensure that all SaaS applications are used securely and that any unauthorized applications (shadow IT) are identified and managed appropriately.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eUnify control over data security policies\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSecurity Service Edge (SSE) solutions can provide unified control over data security policies across your SaaS environment. An \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one\"\u003eSSE platform\u003c/a\u003e integrates various security functions such as a CASB, a Secure Web Gateway (SWG) and Zero Trust Network Access (ZTNA) and should offer single-pane-of-glass visibility across all channels. This approach simplifies the management of security policies and ensures consistent enforcement across all applications and services. By adopting SSE, you can streamline your security operations and enhance the overall security posture of your SaaS product.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eSaaS data security offers a strategy for success\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy implementing these seven SaaS data security best practices, you can promote the safety of your expanding roster of SaaS products and protect sensitive data from cyber threats. Prioritizing data security not only safeguards your operations but also builds trust with your customers, ensuring the long-term health of your business. Adopting a streamlined and proactive strategy will help you reap the benefits of SaaS without falling prey to dangerous vulnerabilities.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAre you ready to learn more about how SSE protects access to SaaS products? The ease of implementation and the collaborative capabilities that SaaS products offer make them indispensable for most operations. But adopting SaaS tools is only sustainable if you have the right security measures in place to prevent data breaches.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere you’ll find seven SaaS data security best practices to promote safety and productivity for your company. The best practices covered below are:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003eEnforce strong, centralized authentication\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eProactively strengthen your SaaS security posture\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eImplement a Data Loss Prevention (DLP) solution\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eMonitor users with behavioral analytics\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eLeverage AI/ML for advanced capabilities\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUse a CASB to protect SaaS access and discover shadow IT\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eUnify control over data security policies\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ch2\u003eEnforce strong, centralized authentication\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eA crucial early step for ensuring SaaS data security is to use robust and consistent authentication mechanisms. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) provides an additional layer of security by requiring users to provide two or more verification factors to gain access.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis significantly reduces the risk of unauthorized access, even if a user’s password is compromised. Identity Access Management (IAM) tools further help by managing user identities and access levels, ensuring that only authorized individuals can access sensitive data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eProactively strengthen your SaaS security posture\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo stay ahead of potential threats, it’s vital to proactively maintain a strong SaaS security posture. This purpose can be accomplished by adopting tools such as \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/data-security-posture-management-dspm\"\u003eData Security Posture Management (DSPM)\u003c/a\u003e – you also may encounter products with broadly overlapping capabilities under category names like Cloud Security Posture Management (CSPM), SaaS Security Posture Management (SSPM) and AI Security Posture Management (AISPM).\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese tools help identify and mitigate security risks by continuously monitoring and assessing your security posture. They provide insights into vulnerabilities and misconfigurations, enabling you to take corrective actions before they can be exploited by attackers.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ch2\u003eImplement a Data Loss Prevention (DLP) solution\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eData Loss Prevention (DLP) solutions are essential for protecting sensitive data from unauthorized access and accidental leaks. A DLP tool monitors and controls data transfers across your network, ensuring that sensitive information is not shared or accessed inappropriately.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy implementing an \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one-data-security\"\u003eeffective DLP solution\u003c/a\u003e, you can enforce data security policies, detect potential breaches and prevent data exfiltration. This is particularly important for SaaS products that handle large volumes of sensitive customer data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMonitor users with behavioral analytics\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eUtilizing advanced behavioral analytics makes it possible to automatically monitor user activities and detect anomalous behavior. A tool like \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/risk-adaptive-protection\"\u003eForcepoint Risk-Adaptive Protection\u003c/a\u003e that analyzes behavioral patterns can identify potential security threats such as insider attacks or compromised accounts. This approach allows you to respond to threats in real time, minimizing the risk of data breaches. Implementing Risk-Adaptive Protection as part of your SaaS data security strategy helps ensure that any suspicious activities are quickly flagged and addressed.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eLeverage AI/ML for advanced capabilities\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eArtificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML) provide groundbreaking functionality to enhance SaaS data security, through both automation and improved processes. For instance, the \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/ai-mesh\"\u003eAI Mesh\u003c/a\u003e model employed by Forcepoint DSPM can rapidly and accurately identify sensitive data across your organization, allowing you to eliminate ROT (Redundant, Obsolete or Trivial) data that can easily lead to breaches.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eUse a CASB to protect SaaS access and discover shadow IT\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eCloud Access Security Brokers (CASBs) are essential for protecting access to your SaaS applications. A CASB will provide visibility and control over data and user activities across cloud services. They help enforce security policies, detect unauthorized access and prevent data breaches.\u0026nbsp;\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy using a \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/casb-cloud-access-security-broker\"\u003eleading CASB\u003c/a\u003e, you can ensure that all SaaS applications are used securely and that any unauthorized applications (shadow IT) are identified and managed appropriately.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eUnify control over data security policies\u003cstrong\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eSecurity Service Edge (SSE) solutions can provide unified control over data security policies across your SaaS environment. An \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/forcepoint-one\"\u003eSSE platform\u003c/a\u003e integrates various security functions such as a CASB, a Secure Web Gateway (SWG) and Zero Trust Network Access (ZTNA) and should offer single-pane-of-glass visibility across all channels. This approach simplifies the management of security policies and ensures consistent enforcement across all applications and services. By adopting SSE, you can streamline your security operations and enhance the overall security posture of your SaaS product.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eSaaS data security offers a strategy for success\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy implementing these seven SaaS data security best practices, you can promote the safety of your expanding roster of SaaS products and protect sensitive data from cyber threats. Prioritizing data security not only safeguards your operations but also builds trust with your customers, ensuring the long-term health of your business. Adopting a streamlined and proactive strategy will help you reap the benefits of SaaS without falling prey to dangerous vulnerabilities.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAre you ready to learn more about how SSE protects access to SaaS products? Download the Gartner® report, \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/resources/industry-analyst-reports/gartner-saas-security-with-security-service-edge\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e6 Steps for Securing Access to SaaS Using the Security Service Edge\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","format":"full_html"},"pgBackgroundImage":null,"paragraphClasses":null,"paragraphFullWidth":false}],"metatag":[{"__typename":"MetaTagValue","tag":"meta","attributes":{"content":"Stop Breaches With 7 SaaS Data Security Best Practices - U\u003c/span\u003enderstanding what these regulations are for, how far they go (or do not go) and who they apply to is an often overlooked first step in true AI adoption.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMuch Ado About Something\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eLegislation is spurring companies to be more thoughtful about AI and how it impacts end users. Companies bear the responsibility of ensuring data is in safe hands as with any other application, and users must retain control over what data is fed to AI – in case they want to delete it.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eMany companies put a user interface on AI and expect that \u003cem\u003evoila\u003c/em\u003e – Series A funding is right around the corner. But for a lot of these startups, the entire back end of the product is open source, and the AI is training on that data.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith AI legislation in mind, organizations must retain complete control over data. In some cases, that means making sure that AI is plug-and-play instead of one-size-fits-all. Consider the following:\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eData is a one-way street\u003c/strong\u003e. AI must function as an enterprise, closed-end model.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAI varies by function\u003c/strong\u003e. Evaluate AI investments based on who you are—customer support, software development or marketing, for example. The criticality or sensitivity of the data you share with that AI should reflect the security measures it has in place.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAI must have transparency.\u003c/strong\u003e Document everything and ensure people understand how AI is used within a product. Don’t give out intellectual property but explain how data moves from input to output. Here’s an example of how Forcepoint does this with \u003ca href=\"http://www.forcepoint.com/ai-mesh\"\u003eAI Mesh\u003c/a\u003e.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003eKeep The ‘Off Switch’ in Sight\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cp\u003eMost importantly, companies must become increasingly thoughtful about how AI is integrated into the service stack. This is because on an individual basis, organizations must allow users the ability to request AI be turned off.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eConsider this: if you’ve spent the last year building a brand-new AI chatbot and a piece of legislation provides for users to opt out of it, how will you handle this request? There must be consideration to the workflows in place and how regulations can impact them.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs an example, Forcepoint informs users, both at the prompt window and during the generated output, that they are engaging with AI and before using AI chatbot capabilities provided by Forcepoint.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eForcepoint also provides a listing of our data sub-processors that we use in support of our products and operations. That’s why our AI tools and services are denoted with (*), via our \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/sites/default/files/2024-09/datasheet-forcepoint-sub-processors-list-Sep24-en.pdf\"\u003eForcepoint Sub-processor List\u003c/a\u003e on our website.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-10/impact-of-legislation-on-ai.jpg\"\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp class=\"text-align-center\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/p\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;\"\u003eBy chatting, you consent to the processing of your data and the chat being stored according to Forcepoint's\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/company/privacy-policy\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;\"\u003ePrivacy Policy\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-family:\u0026quot;Aptos\u0026quot;,sans-serif;font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;\"\u003e. Please be aware this chatbot uses Generative Artificial Intelligence to process and respond to questions. Chatbot responses may contain errors, please verify accuracy of the output.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis binary usage of AI will become the standard in 2025 and beyond as enterprises continue to grapple with how to provide AI-powered software services while still providing the option for users to opt out of the AI portion of those services.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBesides opt-out, organizations must also have the ability to identify the specific individuals interacting with AI and the personal data they share within it. \u003ca href=\"https://www.forcepoint.com/product/data-security-posture-management-dspm\"\u003eData Security Posture Management\u003c/a\u003e (DSPM) helps here by identifying and classifying the data you have so you can monitor interactions with platforms like ChatGPT Enterprise to ensure end-user activity doesn’t result in non-compliance.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUsers are eager to take advantage of AI and companies are right to be skating toward the puck of innovation. However, software vendors must account for legislation in the design of their services sooner rather than later.\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003cspan\u003e\u003co:p\u003e\u003c/o:p\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e","processed":"\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong
